  55. I always wondered how my colleague had such voluminous curls... so I finally asked her. When she told me hot rollers, the memories of my repressed childhood nightmares came to mind. I immediately pictured that family photo where my mother fixed my hair in hot rollers only to have my bob look like a mushroom. Now that I actually know how to put them in correctly, I thought, I should give it another go. After searching for the best rollers I couldn't believe I kept running into this set... I thought for sure I would be spending an obscene amount for a best set. Reluctantly I ordered but immediately tested them the day they arrived. My life as we know it has changed forever. My hair looks perfect every time and I actually spend way less time than I ever did with a blow dryer and round brush on my super long locks. I have long baby fine hair that is layered so I find it most difficult to achieve the perfect curl (and actually last all day) - also being that my hair is straight as a board. Here's the secret... blow dry your hair (upside down for more volume)... There are 8 medium size rollers and 4 large in this set so... Start at the bottom of your hair line with three rolling under - One behind each ear then one in the center back (hairspray - tresemme is the lightest and best). Then do another row of three rolled under again (medium) above the same areas of the medium size. For the last two medium rollers - put on either side of your head at your temples rolling under. You should now have a wide row of hair on top - sort of like a wide mohawk... Start with the back and section evenly one at a time working forward to your face. Roll the pieces back away from your face. Douse with hairspray.. Let it completely cool (Put your makeup on, drink your coffee, relax!).. Remove from the bottom hairline up gently turning the rollers with the curl as you unwind it. DON'T BRUSH! Just work out your natural part with your fingers only touching your scalp. Spray and you're done!You're welcome!

DO NOT straighten your hair before curling because although it may still work you are decreasing your chances of a perfect result. It takes practice to be able to use these properly, and yes the clips could be more convenient to use, but they are doable. Although the curlers can heat up in less than five minutes, I would give them at least ten. The longer they heat, the better they will hold your hair. Fifteen to twenty minutes in your hair is all the time you need. I honestly think that the people who gave this product bad reviews are just impatient and are expecting a perfect product, when one just does not exist in this category. They heat up very quickly, and create beautiful body and curls. I have been reading reviews here from people who commented that the clips were hard to use or that the rollers fell out of their hair. This is because the clips were not inserted properly around the roller. Point the clip prong end first directly at your scalp around the roller and then pivot the clip around the roller. The rollers will be held tightly using this method. Other commenters mentioned they ended up with no curl. As a cosmetologist I can tell you that dirty hair will not hold a curl. You must also wait until the rollers have completely cooled before taking them out. This would seem obvious to most people. Anyway, I LOVE these rollers. I have used them everyday since receiving them for Christmas and everyone has commented on my gorgeous hair. I myself have to admit I am able to create bouncy sexy curls and waves with these rollers and could not be more pleased. The clips could be easer to use if they were the \\"clamp\\" type. However, the ones that come with the set are perfectly fine if you know how to use them. These rollers will keep me growing longer hair now that I can create the same styles I see in fashion without the bother of having to use a curling iron. Finally, I suceed in getting the hair to stay in the roller (the roller is rolled up to the area of my ear, just trying to curl in the ends, not all the way to the root). Then I reach for a pin and get it on there all right, begin work on the next clump of hair when the first roller starts to creep it's way down, no longer horizontal, but becoming more vertical.<br />Solution? I went to Meijer's and found some roller hinge-type clips for 5 bucks in a bag of 10. Sure makes a difference. Also, I am having trouble rolling up the back hair. Any tips there? My overall hair length uncurled is just below shoulder length. Hope this helps. I sure wish that Conair had included hinge clips with this set; the pins are practically useless for my fine hair.

  145. I have long hair, maybe about an inch past my bra strap in the back. It's not thick or thin. If I don't blow dry it, it ends up partially wavy/straight/curly, and frizzy (not nice looking!). It's a pain to always have to blow dry it, and my hair lacks volume. I see people with gorgeous, full hair, and they don't even have to blow dry it. Why can't my hair be like that?! For whatever reason, I thought of trying hair rollers... Over the past two weeks, or so, I've tried several different types of hair products, and combinations of them, to use with the hair rollers until I found what works for me. I thought I would share in case it helps anyone else. When I first started using the rollers, it would look great initially, but then it would fall out within 20 minutes. Sometimes, if I used the curlers when the curlers claimed to be ready (after only two minutes of heating), it wouldn't hardly leave a curl in my hair. But I've figured out what works for me. Hopefully it'll be helpful to some people. And, the new way I do my hair, I never have to blow dry it anymore. It's awesome! Here's what I do: - Before bed, I shower. - I towel dry my hair, and then add 3-4 squirts of \\"Big and Sexy Blow Dry and Volume Gel\\" (I've tried different gels, and none have worked as well as this one!) - Then I go to bed with wet hair and wake up with a mess of hair. It's fun because I know it's going to look good in about 30 minutes. - Turn on my curlers for AT LEAST 15 minutes before I will use them (otherwise it's not hot enough). If you leave them on for a long time before using them, it does get pretty hot. Sometimes it's almost too hot to hold them. So, about the time I'm ready to use them, I'll open the lid for a minute or two before using them, and it helps not burn my fingers. - I put the curlers in my hair like this video says to do (thanks to the previous poster who left this video! It's helped tremendously). Here's the video (in case the link gets deleted, the name of the you tube video is \\"Beauty How To: Soft, Sexy Curls with Hot Rollers\\". You can search on you tube for it): <...> - With each bunch of hair that I gather to put in a roller, I spray it first with \\"Tresemme Thermal Creations Heat Tamer Protective Spray\\". I spray it on both sides of my hair as I hold it up getting ready to put it in the roller. I make sure to spray the whole strand. This is important because at first I only did one side, and I also tried using less of the spray. But in order to get it to work and hold the curl, I needed more. I also tried doing this without the gel, and it didn't work. I was worried if I put too much in, it wouldn't dry in time, but it does. (I make it lightly damp, not dripping or anything!) - I use a combo of clips. As I was buying this product, I saw that some people like the \\"claw\\" clips and other people prefer the wire clips. I had no idea what I would prefer, so I went ahead and bought the claw clips so I had the choice. I use both types. On the top of my head, all of them are claw clips that I use (make sure you put them on correctly, and they won't let your hair fall out of the roller or flop around on your head.) The claw clips I bought are the Conair SPC10X Super Clips. It only comes with 10, but I use 12 hair rollers, so at least two are always wire clips. I don't use the wire clips on the top of my head, but I will use them around the sides/back. I've found them to work great too. I can't decide if I like the claw clips or the wire clips better. The video shows you how to use both of them. Sometimes I have to use two wire clips on the same roller - coming from both directions - and it'll help hold the roller still and in place. My only complaint is that with my hair (maybe other people's hair is different), I need two more rollers. When you watch the video, you see how she does the top, then when you go to the sides, there are two \\"special\\" spots on each side ofyour head that she says to go ahead and put rollers in. I don't have enough rollers to do those spots. So, I don't. It still works good. But two more rollers would have been nice! It's not enough of a problem for mark it down from 5 stars, though. - Anyway, once it's all on, I just wait until all the rollers are no longer warm. - Then, I take my hair out. I start with the bottom/back first and work my way up. I unroll them carefully so they keep the curl that was made. - Once I get all of the rollers out, I will spray it with \\"Big Sexy Hair Spray & Play Volumizing Hairspray\\". (I've tried different hairsprays, and for whatever reason, they really don't work as well.) Often on the top of my head, I feel like it's a bit flat - like I need more volume up there to balance out the curls and make it look really nice and full. My hair has a tendency to be really flat. I found this awesome powder stuff that works AMAZING. It's called \\"Big Sexy Hair Powder Play Volumizing & Texturizing Powder\\". I pour a little powder onto my fingers, flip my head down, and work it in my roots. I'll do it a few times in different spots to get everywhere that needs some lift. I don't know how or why it works, but it adds strength and lift to the hair. It's awesome stuff. I love it! My hair is no longer flat. It's lifting up and full looking - it looks MUCH thicker. I promise I don't work for Big & Sexy hair products! hehe. I realize most of the products I'm suggesting are from them. I've never even heard of these Big & Sexy products until the last couple weeks, and for those will bodiless hair - these are THE products to try! I can't tell you how excited I've been to learn about them. They are a dream come true for my type of hair! And, they really work. It's like magic. I'm excited because after I have a baby, I lose a lot of hair, and it gets thin looking up on top (I HATE it, though my husband claims he can't tell at all). These products are a life saver (or will be, once this new baby is born!). Anyway, then I do whatever I want with the curls - whether I want to work them out a bit or not. It's important to be aware that these cause BIG, LOOSE curls (that stay, if your hair is like mine, and you do what I suggested). They are not going to be small curls since the rollers are so big. They just give a whole lot of body and big curls. I spray them a few different times with the Big & Sexy hairspray. These products have worked awesome for me with the rollers. I like to pull back just my bangs and clip them back (I don't really have bangs. They are as long as the rest of my hair). Then the curls look great. It's SO FUN to have my hair looking fuller and thicker. It's something I've never had. As I said, I don't have thin hair (unless it's after having a baby), but I do have flat hair. I LOVE these rollers in combo with the hair products I mentioned. I tried other hair products/combos, and they didn't do the same thing at all. I love having full, thick looking hair. It's so fun to do my hair every morning! If you don't want actual curls, you can work them out, or just leave the curlers in for a shorter amount of time (or don't let them heat up so long). I might come back and show before/after pics, but I haven't gotten there yet. If you're not having luck, try different hair products. Sometimes it's worth paying for professional products because they really work better if you're needing something specific.

I love that this set includes different sized rollers to create a more natural-look.<br /><br />Things I've learned about using this set and rollers in general:<br />1. For hair sections around your face, I read that you're supposed to wrap the hair away from your face if that makes sense.<br />4.   583. I got these today and I've never used rollers before, but I have frizzy, super thick, super long hair and I'm tired of wasting an hour of every other day using a flat iron. I was putting them in upside down. The little bent part has to go UNDER the roller. Then, they work just fine. It took me about an hour to do the first two, but after I educated myself, it took about 10 minutes to redo my entire head. If you have hair close to your waist, you have to wrap some of your hair around the roller. It does not have to be flat like when you use an iron - just twist it and wrap it around then roll the thing toward your head. And if you have little frizzies near your scalp like I do, don't worry about them - the heat will eventually get to those little boogers.<br /><br />I am honestly impressed.
